[ChatDev is a software company powered by multiple intelligent agents, such as chief executive officer, chief human resources officer, chief product officer, chief technology officer, etc, with a multi-agent organizational structure and the mission of 'changing the digital world through programming'.

To complete the task, You must write a response that appropriately solves the requested instruction based on your expertise and customer's needs.]

To create a personalized lesson roadmap for advancing Python skills from intermediate to advanced, we'll develop a Python application with a graphical user interface (GUI) using the `tkinter` library. This application will allow users to interactively engage with the lesson roadmap, participate in live sessions, complete practical exercises, and receive feedback.

### Core Classes and Functions

1. **MainApp**: The main application class that initializes the GUI and manages the overall flow.
   - `__init__(self)`: Initializes the main application window.
   - `run(self)`: Starts the main loop of the application.

2. **LessonRoadmap**: Manages the lesson roadmap content.
   - `load_roadmap(self)`: Loads the lesson roadmap from a file or database.
   - `display_roadmap(self)`: Displays the roadmap in the GUI.

3. **InteractiveSession**: Handles live interactive sessions.
   - `schedule_session(self)`: Allows users to schedule a live session.
   - `join_session(self)`: Provides functionality to join a live session.

4. **ExerciseManager**: Manages practical exercises and feedback.
   - `load_exercises(self)`: Loads exercises from a file or database.
   - `submit_exercise(self)`: Allows users to submit exercises for feedback.
   - `provide_feedback(self)`: Provides feedback on submitted exercises.

5. **SupportManager**: Manages support for follow-up questions.
   - `ask_question(self)`: Allows users to ask follow-up questions.
   - `provide_answer(self)`: Provides answers to user questions.

### File Structure

1. `main.py`: Contains the MainApp class and initializes the application.
2. `lesson_roadmap.py`: Contains the LessonRoadmap class.
3. `interactive_session.py`: Contains the InteractiveSession class.
4. `exercise_manager.py`: Contains the ExerciseManager class.
5. `support_manager.py`: Contains the SupportManager class.

Let's start with the implementation of each file.

#### main.py

```python
'''

Main application file that initializes and runs the Python skill advancement application.

'''

import tkinter as tk
from lesson_roadmap import LessonRoadmap
from interactive_session import InteractiveSession
from exercise_manager import ExerciseManager
from support_manager import SupportManager

class MainApp:
    def __init__(self):
        self.root = tk.Tk()
        self.root.title("Python Skill Advancement")
        
        # Initialize components
        self.lesson_roadmap = LessonRoadmap(self.root)
        self.interactive_session = InteractiveSession(self.root)
        self.exercise_manager = ExerciseManager(self.root)
        self.support_manager = SupportManager(self.root)
        
        # Layout setup
        self.setup_ui()

    def setup_ui(self):
        # Setup UI components
        self.lesson_roadmap.display_roadmap()
        self.interactive_session.setup_ui()
        self.exercise_manager.setup_ui()
        self.support_manager.setup_ui()

    def run(self):
        self.root.mainloop()

if __name__ == "__main__":
    app = MainApp()
    app.run()
```

#### lesson_roadmap.py

```python
'''

Manages the lesson roadmap content and displays it in the GUI.

'''

import tkinter as tk

class LessonRoadmap:
    def __init__(self, master):
        self.master = master
        self.frame = tk.Frame(self.master)
        self.frame.pack()

    def load_roadmap(self):
        # Load roadmap from a file or database
        self.roadmap = [
            "1. Advanced Data Structures",
            "2. Object-Oriented Programming",
            "3. Functional Programming",
            "4. Concurrency and Parallelism",
            "5. Advanced Libraries and Frameworks",
            "6. Testing and Debugging",
            "7. Performance Optimization"
        ]

    def display_roadmap(self):
        self.load_roadmap()
        tk.Label(self.frame, text="Lesson Roadmap", font=("Arial", 16)).pack()
        for lesson in self.roadmap:
            tk.Label(self.frame, text=lesson).pack()
```

**[Seminar Conclusion]**:

 To create a personalized lesson roadmap for advancing Python skills from intermediate to advanced, we'll develop a Python application with a graphical user interface (GUI) using the `tkinter` library. This application will allow users to interactively engage with the lesson roadmap, participate in live sessions, complete practical exercises, and receive feedback.

### Core Classes and Functions

1. **MainApp**: The main application class that initializes the GUI and manages the overall flow.
   - `__init__(self)`: Initializes the main application window.
   - `run(self)`: Starts the main loop of the application.

2. **LessonRoadmap**: Manages the lesson roadmap content.
   - `load_roadmap(self)`: Loads the lesson roadmap from a file or database.
   - `display_roadmap(self)`: Displays the roadmap in the GUI.

3. **InteractiveSession**: Handles live interactive sessions.
   - `schedule_session(self)`: Allows users to schedule a live session.
   - `join_session(self)`: Provides functionality to join a live session.

4. **ExerciseManager**: Manages practical exercises and feedback.
   - `load_exercises(self)`: Loads exercises from a file or database.
   - `submit_exercise(self)`: Allows users to submit exercises for feedback.
   - `provide_feedback(self)`: Provides feedback on submitted exercises.

5. **SupportManager**: Manages support for follow-up questions.
   - `ask_question(self)`: Allows users to ask follow-up questions.
   - `provide_answer(self)`: Provides answers to user questions.

### File Structure

1. `main.py`: Contains the MainApp class and initializes the application.
2. `lesson_roadmap.py`: Contains the LessonRoadmap class.
3. `interactive_session.py`: Contains the InteractiveSession class.
4. `exercise_manager.py`: Contains the ExerciseManager class.
5. `support_manager.py`: Contains the SupportManager class.

Let's start with the implementation of each file.

```python
import tkinter as tk

from interactive_session import InteractiveSession

from support_manager import SupportManager

        self.lesson_roadmap = LessonRoadmap(self.root)
        self.interactive_session = InteractiveSession(self.root)
        self.exercise_manager = ExerciseManager(self.root)
        self.support_manager = SupportManager(self.root)

        self.interactive_session.setup_ui()
        self.exercise_manager.setup_ui()
```

```python
'''
```
```python
Main application file that initializes and runs the Python skill advancement application.
'''
import tkinter as tk
from lesson_roadmap import LessonRoadmap
from interactive_session import InteractiveSession
from exercise_manager import ExerciseManager
from support_manager import SupportManager
class MainApp:
    def __init__(self):
        self.root = tk.Tk()
        self.root.title("Python Skill Advancement")
        # Initialize components
        self.lesson_roadmap = LessonRoadmap(self.root)
        self.interactive_session = InteractiveSession(self.root)
        self.exercise_manager = ExerciseManager(self.root)
        self.support_manager = SupportManager(self.root)
        # Layout setup
        self.setup_ui()
    def setup_ui(self):
        # Setup UI components
        self.lesson_roadmap.display_roadmap()
        self.interactive_session.setup_ui()
        self.exercise_manager.setup_ui()
        self.support_manager.setup_ui()
    def run(self):
        self.root.mainloop()
if __name__ == "__main__":
    app = MainApp()
    app.run()
```

lesson_roadmap.py
```python
'''
Manages the lesson roadmap content and displays it in the GUI.
'''
import tkinter as tk
class LessonRoadmap:
    def __init__(self, master):
        self.master = master
        self.frame = tk.Frame(self.master)
        self.frame.pack()
    def load_roadmap(self):
        # Load roadmap from a file or database
        self.roadmap = [
            "1. Advanced Data Structures",
            "2. Object-Oriented Programming",
            "3. Functional Programming",
            "4. Concurrency and Parallelism",
            "5. Advanced Libraries and Frameworks",
            "6. Testing and Debugging",
            "7. Performance Optimization"
        ]
    def display_roadmap(self):
        self.load_roadmap()
        tk.Label(self.frame, text="Lesson Roadmap", font=("Arial", 16)).pack()
        for lesson in self.roadmap:
            tk.Label(self.frame, text=lesson).pack()
```

```python
'''

class InteractiveSession:
    def __init__(self, master):
        self.master = master

        self.frame.pack()
    def setup_ui(self):
        tk.Label(self.frame, text="Interactive Sessions", font=("Arial", 16)).pack()
        tk.Button(self.frame, text="Schedule Session", command=self.schedule_session).pack()
        tk.Button(self.frame, text="Join Session", command=self.join_session).pack()
    def schedule_session(self):
        # Logic to schedule a session
        print("Session scheduled.")
    def join_session(self):
        # Logic to join a session
        print("Joined session.")
```

Here is a new customer's task: Please help me create a personalized lesson roadmap for advancing Python skills from intermediate to advanced, incorporating live interactive sessions, practical exercises with feedback, and support for follow-up questions..
To complete the task, you must write a response that appropriately solves the requested instruction based on your expertise and customer's needs.]

main.py
```python
'''
Main application file that initializes and runs the Python skill advancement application.
'''
import tkinter as tk
from lesson_roadmap import LessonRoadmap
from interactive_session import InteractiveSession
from exercise_manager import ExerciseManager
from support_manager import SupportManager

class MainApp:
    def __init__(self):
        self.root = tk.Tk()
        self.root.title("Python Skill Advancement")
        # Initialize components
        self.lesson_roadmap = LessonRoadmap(self.root)
        self.interactive_session = InteractiveSession(self.root)
        self.exercise_manager = ExerciseManager(self.root)
        self.support_manager = SupportManager(self.root)
        # Layout setup
        self.setup_ui()

    def setup_ui(self):
        # Setup UI components
        self.lesson_roadmap.display_roadmap()
        self.interactive_session.setup_ui()
        self.exercise_manager.setup_ui()
        self.support_manager.setup_ui()

    def run(self):
        self.root.mainloop()

if __name__ == "__main__":
    app = MainApp()
    app.run()
```

lesson_roadmap.py
```python
'''
Manages the lesson roadmap content and displays it in the GUI.
'''
import tkinter as tk

class LessonRoadmap:
    def __init__(self, master):
        self.master = master
        self.frame = tk.Frame(self.master)
        self.frame.pack()

    def load_roadmap(self):
        # Load roadmap from a file or database
        self.roadmap = [
            "1. Advanced Data Structures",
            "2. Object-Oriented Programming",
            "3. Functional Programming",
            "4. Concurrency and Parallelism",
            "5. Advanced Libraries and Frameworks",
            "6. Testing and Debugging",
            "7. Performance Optimization"
        ]

    def display_roadmap(self):
        self.load_roadmap()
        tk.Label(self.frame, text="Lesson Roadmap", font=("Arial", 16)).pack()
        for lesson in self.roadmap:
            tk.Label(self.frame, text=lesson).pack()
```

interactive_session.py
```python
'''
Handles live interactive sessions, allowing users to schedule and join sessions.
'''
import tkinter as tk
import sqlite3

class InteractiveSession:
    def __init__(self, master):
        self.master = master
        self.frame = tk.Frame(self.master)
        self.frame.pack()
        self.db_connection = sqlite3.connect('sessions.db')
        self.create_table()

    def create_table(self):
        # Create table for sessions if it doesn't exist
        with self.db_connection:
            self.db_connection.execute('''
                CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS sessions (
                    id INTEGER PRIMARY KEY AUTOINCREMENT,
                    session_name TEXT NOT NULL
                )
            ''')

    def setup_ui(self):
        tk.Label(self.frame, text="Interactive Sessions", font=("Arial", 16)).pack()
        tk.Button(self.frame, text="Schedule Session", command=self.schedule_session).pack()
        tk.Button(self.frame, text="Join Session", command=self.join_session).pack()

    def schedule_session(self):
        # Logic to schedule a session
        session_name = "New Session"
        with self.db_connection:
            self.db_connection.execute('INSERT INTO sessions (session_name) VALUES (?)', (session_name,))
        print("Session scheduled.")

    def join_session(self):
        # Logic to join a session
        cursor = self.db_connection.cursor()
        cursor.execute('SELECT * FROM sessions')
        sessions = cursor.fetchall()
        if sessions:
            print("Joined session:", sessions[0][1])
        else:
            print("No sessions available to join.")
```

exercise_manager.py
```python
'''
Manages practical exercises and feedback, allowing users to submit exercises and receive feedback.
'''
import tkinter as tk
import sqlite3

class ExerciseManager:
    def __init__(self, master):
        self.master = master
        self.frame = tk.Frame(self.master)
        self.frame.pack()
        self.db_connection = sqlite3.connect('exercises.db')
        self.create_table()

    def create_table(self):
        # Create table for exercises if it doesn't exist
        with self.db_connection:
            self.db_connection.execute('''
                CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS exercises (
                    id INTEGER PRIMARY KEY AUTOINCREMENT,
                    exercise_name TEXT NOT NULL,
                    feedback TEXT
                )
            ''')

    def setup_ui(self):
        tk.Label(self.frame, text="Exercises", font=("Arial", 16)).pack()
        tk.Button(self.frame, text="Submit Exercise", command=self.submit_exercise).pack()
        tk.Button(self.frame, text="Get Feedback", command=self.provide_feedback).pack()

    def submit_exercise(self):
        # Logic to submit an exercise
        exercise_name = "Exercise 1"
        with self.db_connection:
            self.db_connection.execute('INSERT INTO exercises (exercise_name) VALUES (?)', (exercise_name,))
        print("Exercise submitted.")

    def provide_feedback(self):
        # Logic to provide feedback
        cursor = self.db_connection.cursor()
        cursor.execute('SELECT * FROM exercises')
        exercises = cursor.fetchall()
        if exercises:
            feedback = "Good job!"
            with self.db_connection:
                self.db_connection.execute('UPDATE exercises SET feedback = ? WHERE id = ?', (feedback, exercises[0][0]))
            print("Feedback provided:", feedback)
        else:
            print("No exercises available for feedback.")
```

support_manager.py
```python
'''
Manages support for follow-up questions, allowing users to ask questions and receive answers.
'''
import tkinter as tk
import sqlite3

class SupportManager:
    def __init__(self, master):
        self.master = master
        self.frame = tk.Frame(self.master)
        self.frame.pack()
        self.db_connection = sqlite3.connect('support.db')
        self.create_table()

    def create_table(self):
        # Create table for support questions if it doesn't exist
        with self.db_connection:
            self.db_connection.execute('''
                CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS support (
                    id INTEGER PRIMARY KEY AUTOINCREMENT,
                    question TEXT NOT NULL,
                    answer TEXT
                )
            ''')

    def setup_ui(self):
        tk.Label(self.frame, text="Support", font=("Arial", 16)).pack()
        tk.Button(self.frame, text="Ask Question", command=self.ask_question).pack()
        tk.Button(self.frame, text="Get Answer", command=self.provide_answer).pack()

    def ask_question(self):
        # Logic to ask a question
        question = "What is Python?"
        with self.db_connection:
            self.db_connection.execute('INSERT INTO support (question) VALUES (?)', (question,))
        print("Question asked.")

    def provide_answer(self):
        # Logic to provide an answer
        cursor = self.db_connection.cursor()
        cursor.execute('SELECT * FROM support')
        questions = cursor.fetchall()
        if questions:
            answer = "Python is a programming language."
            with self.db_connection:
                self.db_connection.execute('UPDATE support SET answer = ? WHERE id = ?', (answer, questions[0][0]))
            print("Answer provided:", answer)
        else:
            print("No questions available for answers.")
```

```python
'''
```

```python
import tkinter as tk
import sqlite3

class SupportManager:
    def __init__(self, master):
        self.master = master
        self.frame = tk.Frame(self.master)
        self.frame.pack()
        self.db_connection = sqlite3.connect('support.db')
        self.create_table()

    def create_table(self):
        # Create table for support questions if it doesn't exist
        with self.db_connection:
            self.db_connection.execute('''
                CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS support (
                    id INTEGER PRIMARY KEY AUTOINCREMENT,
                    question TEXT NOT NULL,
                    answer TEXT
                )
            ''')

    def setup_ui(self):
        tk.Label(self.frame, text="Support", font=("Arial", 16)).pack()
        tk.Button(self.frame, text="Ask Question", command=self.ask_question).pack()
        tk.Button(self.frame, text="Get Answer", command=self.provide_answer).pack()

    def ask_question(self):
        # Logic to ask a question
        question = "What is Python?"
        with self.db_connection:
            self.db_connection.execute('INSERT INTO support (question) VALUES (?)', (question,))
        print("Question asked.")

    def provide_answer(self):
        # Logic to provide an answer
        cursor = self.db_connection.cursor()
        cursor.execute('SELECT * FROM support')
        questions = cursor.fetchall()
        if questions:
            answer = "Python is a programming language."
            with self.db_connection:
                self.db_connection.execute('UPDATE support SET answer = ? WHERE id = ?', (answer, questions[0][0]))
            print("Answer provided:", answer)
        else:
            print("No questions available for answers.")
```

```python
'''
Main application file that initializes and runs the Python skill advancement application.
'''
import tkinter as tk
from lesson_roadmap import LessonRoadmap
from interactive_session import InteractiveSession
from exercise_manager import ExerciseManager
from support_manager import SupportManager
class MainApp:
    def __init__(self):
        self.root = tk.Tk()
        self.root.title("Python Skill Advancement")
        # Initialize components
        self.lesson_roadmap = LessonRoadmap(self.root)
        self.interactive_session = InteractiveSession(self.root)
        self.exercise_manager = ExerciseManager(self.root)
        self.support_manager = SupportManager(self.root)
        # Layout setup
        self.setup_ui()
    def setup_ui(self):
        # Setup UI components
        self.lesson_roadmap.display_roadmap()
        self.interactive_session.setup_ui()
        self.exercise_manager.setup_ui()
        self.support_manager.setup_ui()
    def run(self):
        self.root.mainloop()
if __name__ == "__main__":
    app = MainApp()
    app.run()
```

lesson_roadmap.py
```python
'''
Manages the lesson roadmap content and displays it in the GUI.
'''
import tkinter as tk
class LessonRoadmap:
    def __init__(self, master):
        self.master = master
        self.frame = tk.Frame(self.master)
        self.frame.pack()
    def load_roadmap(self):
        # Load roadmap from a file or database
        self.roadmap = [
            "1. Advanced Data Structures",
            "2. Object-Oriented Programming",
            "3. Functional Programming",
            "4. Concurrency and Parallelism",
            "5. Advanced Libraries and Frameworks",
            "6. Testing and Debugging",
            "7. Performance Optimization"
        ]
    def display_roadmap(self):
        self.load_roadmap()
        tk.Label(self.frame, text="Lesson Roadmap", font=("Arial", 16)).pack()
        for lesson in self.roadmap:
            tk.Label(self.frame, text=lesson).pack()
```

interactive_session.py
```python
'''
Handles live interactive sessions, allowing users to schedule and join sessions.
'''
import tkinter as tk
import sqlite3
class InteractiveSession:
    def __init__(self, master):
        self.master = master
        self.frame = tk.Frame(self.master)
        self.frame.pack()
        self.db_connection = sqlite3.connect('sessions.db')
        self.create_table()
    def create_table(self):
        # Create table for sessions if it doesn't exist
        with self.db_connection:
            self.db_connection.execute('''
                CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS sessions (
                    id INTEGER PRIMARY KEY AUTOINCREMENT,
                    session_name TEXT NOT NULL
                )
            ''')
    def setup_ui(self):
        tk.Label(self.frame, text="Interactive Sessions", font=("Arial", 16)).pack()
        tk.Button(self.frame, text="Schedule Session", command=self.schedule_session).pack()
        tk.Button(self.frame, text="Join Session", command=self.join_session).pack()
    def schedule_session(self):
        # Logic to schedule a session
        session_name = "New Session"
        with self.db_connection:
            self.db_connection.execute('INSERT INTO sessions (session_name) VALUES (?)', (session_name,))
        print("Session scheduled.")
    def join_session(self):
        # Logic to join a session
        cursor = self.db_connection.cursor()
        cursor.execute('SELECT * FROM sessions')
        sessions = cursor.fetchall()
        if sessions:
            print("Joined session:", sessions[0][1])
        else:
            print("No sessions available to join.")
```

exercise_manager.py
```python
'''
Manages practical exercises and feedback, allowing users to submit exercises and receive feedback.
'''
import tkinter as tk
import sqlite3
class ExerciseManager:
    def __init__(self, master):
        self.master = master
        self.frame = tk.Frame(self.master)
        self.frame.pack()
        self.db_connection = sqlite3.connect('exercises.db')
        self.create_table()
    def create_table(self):
        # Create table for exercises if it doesn't exist
        with self.db_connection:
            self.db_connection.execute('''
                CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS exercises (
                    id INTEGER PRIMARY KEY AUTOINCREMENT,
                    exercise_name TEXT NOT NULL,
                    feedback TEXT
                )
            ''')
    def setup_ui(self):
        tk.Label(self.frame, text="Exercises", font=("Arial", 16)).pack()
        tk.Button(self.frame, text="Submit Exercise", command=self.submit_exercise).pack()
        tk.Button(self.frame, text="Get Feedback", command=self.provide_feedback).pack()
    def submit_exercise(self):
        # Logic to submit an exercise
        exercise_name = "Exercise 1"
        with self.db_connection:
            self.db_connection.execute('INSERT INTO exercises (exercise_name) VALUES (?)', (exercise_name,))
        print("Exercise submitted.")
    def provide_feedback(self):
        # Logic to provide feedback
        cursor = self.db_connection.cursor()
        cursor.execute('SELECT * FROM exercises')
        exercises = cursor.fetchall()
        if exercises:
            feedback = "Good job!"
            with self.db_connection:
                self.db_connection.execute('UPDATE exercises SET feedback = ? WHERE id = ?', (feedback, exercises[0][0]))
            print("Feedback provided:", feedback)
        else:
            print("No exercises available for feedback.")
```

support_manager.py
```python
'''
Manages support for follow-up questions, allowing users to ask questions and receive answers.
'''
import tkinter as tk
import sqlite3
class SupportManager:
    def __init__(self, master):
        self.master = master
        self.frame = tk.Frame(self.master)
        self.frame.pack()
        self.db_connection = sqlite3.connect('support.db')
        self.create_table()
    def create_table(self):
        # Create table for support questions if it doesn't exist
        with self.db_connection:
            self.db_connection.execute('''
                CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS support (
                    id INTEGER PRIMARY KEY AUTOINCREMENT,
                    question TEXT NOT NULL,
                    answer TEXT
                )
            ''')
    def setup_ui(self):
        tk.Label(self.frame, text="Support", font=("Arial", 16)).pack()
        tk.Button(self.frame, text="Ask Question", command=self.ask_question).pack()
        tk.Button(self.frame, text="Get Answer", command=self.provide_answer).pack()
    def ask_question(self):
        # Logic to ask a question
        question = "What is Python?"
        with self.db_connection:
            self.db_connection.execute('INSERT INTO support (question) VALUES (?)', (question,))
        print("Question asked.")
    def provide_answer(self):
        # Logic to provide an answer
        cursor = self.db_connection.cursor()
        cursor.execute('SELECT * FROM support')
        questions = cursor.fetchall()
        if questions:
            answer = "Python is a programming language."
            with self.db_connection:
                self.db_connection.execute('UPDATE support SET answer = ? WHERE id = ?', (answer, questions[0][0]))
            print("Answer provided:", answer)
        else:
            print("No questions available for answers.")
```

"main.py
```python
'''
Main application file that initializes and runs the Python skill advancement application.
'''
import tkinter as tk
from lesson_roadmap import LessonRoadmap
from interactive_session import InteractiveSession
from exercise_manager import ExerciseManager
from support_manager import SupportManager
class MainApp:
    def __init__(self):
        self.root = tk.Tk()
        self.root.title("Python Skill Advancement")
        # Initialize components
        self.lesson_roadmap = LessonRoadmap(self.root)
        self.interactive_session = InteractiveSession(self.root)
        self.exercise_manager = ExerciseManager(self.root)
        self.support_manager = SupportManager(self.root)
        # Layout setup
        self.setup_ui()
    def setup_ui(self):
        # Setup UI components
        self.lesson_roadmap.display_roadmap()
        self.interactive_session.setup_ui()
        self.exercise_manager.setup_ui()
        self.support_manager.setup_ui()
    def run(self):
        self.root.mainloop()
if __name__ == "__main__":
    app = MainApp()
    app.run()
```

lesson_roadmap.py
```python
'''
Manages the lesson roadmap content and displays it in the GUI.
'''
import tkinter as tk
class LessonRoadmap:
    def __init__(self, master):
        self.master = master
        self.frame = tk.Frame(self.master)
        self.frame.pack()
    def load_roadmap(self):
        # Load roadmap from a file or database
        self.roadmap = [
            "1. Advanced Data Structures",
            "2. Object-Oriented Programming",
            "3. Functional Programming",
            "4. Concurrency and Parallelism",
            "5. Advanced Libraries and Frameworks",
            "6. Testing and Debugging",
            "7. Performance Optimization"
        ]
    def display_roadmap(self):
        self.load_roadmap()
        tk.Label(self.frame, text="Lesson Roadmap", font=("Arial", 16)).pack()
        for lesson in self.roadmap:
            tk.Label(self.frame, text=lesson).pack()
```

interactive_session.py
```python
'''
Handles live interactive sessions, allowing users to schedule and join sessions.
'''
import tkinter as tk
import sqlite3
class InteractiveSession:
    def __init__(self, master):
        self.master = master
        self.frame = tk.Frame(self.master)
        self.frame.pack()
        self.db_connection = sqlite3.connect('sessions.db')
        self.create_table()
    def create_table(self):
        # Create table for sessions if it doesn't exist
        with self.db_connection:
            self.db_connection.execute('''
                CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS sessions (
                    id INTEGER PRIMARY KEY AUTOINCREMENT,
                    session_name TEXT NOT NULL
                )
            ''')
    def setup_ui(self):
        tk.Label(self.frame, text="Interactive Sessions", font=("Arial", 16)).pack()
        tk.Button(self.frame, text="Schedule Session", command=self.schedule_session).pack()
        tk.Button(self.frame, text="Join Session", command=self.join_session).pack()
    def schedule_session(self):
        # Logic to schedule a session
        session_name = "New Session"
        with self.db_connection:
            self.db_connection.execute('INSERT INTO sessions (session_name) VALUES (?)', (session_name,))
        print("Session scheduled.")
    def join_session(self):
        # Logic to join a session
        cursor = self.db_connection.cursor()
        cursor.execute('SELECT * FROM sessions')
        sessions = cursor.fetchall()
        if sessions:
            print("Joined session:", sessions[0][1])
        else:
            print("No sessions available to join.")
```

exercise_manager.py
```python
'''
Manages practical exercises and feedback, allowing users to submit exercises and receive feedback.
'''
import tkinter as tk
import sqlite3
class ExerciseManager:
    def __init__(self, master):
        self.master = master
        self.frame = tk.Frame(self.master)
        self.frame.pack()
        self.db_connection = sqlite3.connect('exercises.db')
        self.create_table()
    def create_table(self):
        # Create table for exercises if it doesn't exist
        with self.db_connection:
            self.db_connection.execute('''
                CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS exercises (
                    id INTEGER PRIMARY KEY AUTOINCREMENT,
                    exercise_name TEXT NOT NULL,
                    feedback TEXT
                )
            ''')
    def setup_ui(self):
        tk.Label(self.frame, text="Exercises", font=("Arial", 16)).pack()
        tk.Button(self.frame, text="Submit Exercise", command=self.submit_exercise).pack()
        tk.Button(self.frame, text="Get Feedback", command=self.provide_feedback).pack()
    def submit_exercise(self):
        # Logic to submit an exercise
        exercise_name = "Exercise 1"
        with self.db_connection:
            self.db_connection.execute('INSERT INTO exercises (exercise_name) VALUES (?)', (exercise_name,))
        print("Exercise submitted.")
    def provide_feedback(self):
        # Logic to provide feedback
        cursor = self.db_connection.cursor()
        cursor.execute('SELECT * FROM exercises')
        exercises = cursor.fetchall()
        if exercises:
            feedback = "Good job!"
            with self.db_connection:
                self.db_connection.execute('UPDATE exercises SET feedback = ? WHERE id = ?', (feedback, exercises[0][0]))
            print("Feedback provided:", feedback)
        else:
            print("No exercises available for feedback.")
```

support_manager.py
```python
'''
Manages support for follow-up questions, allowing users to ask questions and receive answers.
'''
import tkinter as tk
import sqlite3
class SupportManager:
    def __init__(self, master):
        self.master = master
        self.frame = tk.Frame(self.master)
        self.frame.pack()
        self.db_connection = sqlite3.connect('support.db')
        self.create_table()
    def create_table(self):
        # Create table for support questions if it doesn't exist
        with self.db_connection:
            self.db_connection.execute('''
                CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS support (
                    id INTEGER PRIMARY KEY AUTOINCREMENT,
                    question TEXT NOT NULL,
                    answer TEXT
                )
            ''')
    def setup_ui(self):
        tk.Label(self.frame, text="Support", font=("Arial", 16)).pack()
        tk.Button(self.frame, text="Ask Question", command=self.ask_question).pack()
        tk.Button(self.frame, text="Get Answer", command=self.provide_answer).pack()
    def ask_question(self):
        # Logic to ask a question
        question = "What is Python?"
        with self.db_connection:
            self.db_connection.execute('INSERT INTO support (question) VALUES (?)', (question,))
        print("Question asked.")
    def provide_answer(self):
        # Logic to provide an answer
        cursor = self.db_connection.cursor()
        cursor.execute('SELECT * FROM support')
        questions = cursor.fetchall()
        if questions:
            answer = "Python is a programming language."
            with self.db_connection:
                self.db_connection.execute('UPDATE support SET answer = ? WHERE id = ?', (answer, questions[0][0]))
            print("Answer provided:", answer)
        else:
            print("No questions available for answers.")
```

lesson_roadmap.py
```python
'''
Manages the lesson roadmap content and displays it in the GUI.
'''
import tkinter as tk

class LessonRoadmap:
    def __init__(self, master):
        self.master = master
        self.frame = tk.Frame(self.master)
        self.frame.pack()

    def load_roadmap(self):
        # Load roadmap from a file or database
        self.roadmap = [
            "1. Advanced Data Structures",
            "2. Object-Oriented Programming",
            "3. Functional Programming",
            "4. Concurrency and Parallelism",
            "5. Advanced Libraries and Frameworks",
            "6. Testing and Debugging",
            "7. Performance Optimization"
        ]

    def display_roadmap(self):
        self.load_roadmap()
        tk.Label(self.frame, text="Lesson Roadmap", font=("Arial", 16)).pack()
        for lesson in self.roadmap:
            tk.Label(self.frame, text=lesson).pack()
```

interactive_session.py
```python
'''
Handles live interactive sessions, allowing users to schedule and join sessions.
'''
import tkinter as tk
import sqlite3

class InteractiveSession:
    def __init__(self, master):
        self.master = master
        self.frame = tk.Frame(self.master)
        self.frame.pack()
        self.db_connection = sqlite3.connect('sessions.db')
        self.create_table()
        self.session_name_entry = tk.Entry(self.frame)

    def create_table(self):
        # Create table for sessions if it doesn't exist
        with self.db_connection:
            self.db_connection.execute('''
                CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS sessions (
                    id INTEGER PRIMARY KEY AUTOINCREMENT,
                    session_name TEXT NOT NULL
                )
            ''')

    def setup_ui(self):
        tk.Label(self.frame, text="Interactive Sessions", font=("Arial", 16)).pack()
        self.session_name_entry.pack()
        tk.Button(self.frame, text="Schedule Session", command=self.schedule_session).pack()
        tk.Button(self.frame, text="Join Session", command=self.join_session).pack()

    def schedule_session(self):
        # Logic to schedule a session
        session_name = self.session_name_entry.get()
        if session_name:
            with self.db_connection:
                self.db_connection.execute('INSERT INTO sessions (session_name) VALUES (?)', (session_name,))
            print("Session scheduled:", session_name)
        else:
            print("Please enter a session name.")

    def join_session(self):
        # Logic to join a session
        cursor = self.db_connection.cursor()
        cursor.execute('SELECT * FROM sessions')
        sessions = cursor.fetchall()
        if sessions:
            print("Available sessions:")
            for session in sessions:
                print(f"ID: {session[0]}, Name: {session[1]}")
        else:
            print("No sessions available to join.")
```

exercise_manager.py
```python
'''
Manages practical exercises and feedback, allowing users to submit exercises and receive feedback.
'''
import tkinter as tk
import sqlite3

class ExerciseManager:
    def __init__(self, master):
        self.master = master
        self.frame = tk.Frame(self.master)
        self.frame.pack()
        self.db_connection = sqlite3.connect('exercises.db')
        self.create_table()
        self.exercise_name_entry = tk.Entry(self.frame)

    def create_table(self):
        # Create table for exercises if it doesn't exist
        with self.db_connection:
            self.db_connection.execute('''
                CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS exercises (
                    id INTEGER PRIMARY KEY AUTOINCREMENT,
                    exercise_name TEXT NOT NULL,
                    feedback TEXT
                )
            ''')

    def setup_ui(self):
        tk.Label(self.frame, text="Exercises", font=("Arial", 16)).pack()
        self.exercise_name_entry.pack()
        tk.Button(self.frame, text="Submit Exercise", command=self.submit_exercise).pack()
        tk.Button(self.frame, text="Get Feedback", command=self.provide_feedback).pack()

    def submit_exercise(self):
        # Logic to submit an exercise
        exercise_name = self.exercise_name_entry.get()
        if exercise_name:
            with self.db_connection:
                self.db_connection.execute('INSERT INTO exercises (exercise_name) VALUES (?)', (exercise_name,))
            print("Exercise submitted:", exercise_name)
        else:
            print("Please enter an exercise name.")

    def provide_feedback(self):
        # Logic to provide feedback
        cursor = self.db_connection.cursor()
        cursor.execute('SELECT * FROM exercises')
        exercises = cursor.fetchall()
        if exercises:
            for exercise in exercises:
                feedback = "Good job!"
                with self.db_connection:
                    self.db_connection.execute('UPDATE exercises SET feedback = ? WHERE id = ?', (feedback, exercise[0]))
                print(f"Feedback for {exercise[1]}: {feedback}")
        else:
            print("No exercises available for feedback.")
```

support_manager.py
```python
'''
Manages support for follow-up questions, allowing users to ask questions and receive answers.
'''
import tkinter as tk
import sqlite3

class SupportManager:
    def __init__(self, master):
        self.master = master
        self.frame = tk.Frame(self.master)
        self.frame.pack()
        self.db_connection = sqlite3.connect('support.db')
        self.create_table()
        self.question_entry = tk.Entry(self.frame)

    def create_table(self):
        # Create table for support questions if it doesn't exist
        with self.db_connection:
            self.db_connection.execute('''
                CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS support (
                    id INTEGER PRIMARY KEY AUTOINCREMENT,
                    question TEXT NOT NULL,
                    answer TEXT
                )
            ''')

    def setup_ui(self):
        tk.Label(self.frame, text="Support", font=("Arial", 16)).pack()
        self.question_entry.pack()
        tk.Button(self.frame, text="Ask Question", command=self.ask_question).pack()
        tk.Button(self.frame, text="Get Answer", command=self.provide_answer).pack()

    def ask_question(self):
        # Logic to ask a question
        question = self.question_entry.get()
        if question:
            with self.db_connection:
                self.db_connection.execute('INSERT INTO support (question) VALUES (?)', (question,))
            print("Question asked:", question)
        else:
            print("Please enter a question.")

    def provide_answer(self):
        # Logic to provide an answer
        cursor = self.db_connection.cursor()
        cursor.execute('SELECT * FROM support')
        questions = cursor.fetchall()
        if questions:
            for question in questions:
                answer = "Python is a programming language."
                with self.db_connection:
                    self.db_connection.execute('UPDATE support SET answer = ? WHERE id = ?', (answer, question[0]))
                print(f"Answer for '{question[1]}': {answer}")
        else:
            print("No questions available for answers.")
```

```python
class InteractiveSession:

                    id INTEGER PRIMARY KEY AUTOINCREMENT,
                    session_name TEXT NOT NULL
                )
            ''')

    def setup_ui(self):

        tk.Button(self.frame, text="Schedule Session", command=self.schedule_session).pack()
        tk.Button(self.frame, text="Join Session", command=self.join_session).pack()

        # Logic to schedule a session
        session_name = self.session_name_entry.get()
```

```python
'''
Main application file that initializes and runs the Python skill advancement application.
'''
import tkinter as tk
from lesson_roadmap import LessonRoadmap
from interactive_session import InteractiveSession
from exercise_manager import ExerciseManager
from support_manager import SupportManager
class MainApp:
    def __init__(self):
        self.root = tk.Tk()
        self.root.title("Python Skill Advancement")
        # Initialize components
        self.lesson_roadmap = LessonRoadmap(self.root)
        self.interactive_session = InteractiveSession(self.root)
        self.exercise_manager = ExerciseManager(self.root)
        self.support_manager = SupportManager(self.root)
        # Layout setup
        self.setup_ui()
    def setup_ui(self):
        # Setup UI components
        self.lesson_roadmap.display_roadmap()
        self.interactive_session.setup_ui()
        self.exercise_manager.setup_ui()
        self.support_manager.setup_ui()
    def run(self):
        self.root.mainloop()
if __name__ == "__main__":
    app = MainApp()
    app.run()
```

lesson_roadmap.py
```python
'''
Manages the lesson roadmap content and displays it in the GUI.
'''
import tkinter as tk
class LessonRoadmap:
    def __init__(self, master):
        self.master = master
        self.frame = tk.Frame(self.master)
        self.frame.pack()
    def load_roadmap(self):
        # Load roadmap from a file or database
        self.roadmap = [
            "1. Advanced Data Structures",
            "2. Object-Oriented Programming",
            "3. Functional Programming",
            "4. Concurrency and Parallelism",
            "5. Advanced Libraries and Frameworks",
            "6. Testing and Debugging",
            "7. Performance Optimization"
        ]
    def display_roadmap(self):
        self.load_roadmap()
        tk.Label(self.frame, text="Lesson Roadmap", font=("Arial", 16)).pack()
        for lesson in self.roadmap:
            tk.Label(self.frame, text=lesson).pack()
```

interactive_session.py
```python
'''
Handles live interactive sessions, allowing users to schedule and join sessions.
'''
import tkinter as tk
import sqlite3
class InteractiveSession:
    def __init__(self, master):
        self.master = master
        self.frame = tk.Frame(self.master)
        self.frame.pack()
        self.db_connection = sqlite3.connect('sessions.db')
        self.create_table()
        self.session_name_entry = tk.Entry(self.frame)
    def create_table(self):
        # Create table for sessions if it doesn't exist
        with self.db_connection:
            self.db_connection.execute('''
                CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS sessions (
                    id INTEGER PRIMARY KEY AUTOINCREMENT,
                    session_name TEXT NOT NULL
                )
            ''')
    def setup_ui(self):
        tk.Label(self.frame, text="Interactive Sessions", font=("Arial", 16)).pack()
        self.session_name_entry.pack()
        tk.Button(self.frame, text="Schedule Session", command=self.schedule_session).pack()
        tk.Button(self.frame, text="Join Session", command=self.join_session).pack()
    def schedule_session(self):
        # Logic to schedule a session
        session_name = self.session_name_entry.get()
        if session_name:
            with self.db_connection:
                self.db_connection.execute('INSERT INTO sessions (session_name) VALUES (?)', (session_name,))
            print("Session scheduled:", session_name)
        else:
            print("Please enter a session name.")
    def join_session(self):
        # Logic to join a session
        cursor = self.db_connection.cursor()
        cursor.execute('SELECT * FROM sessions')
        sessions = cursor.fetchall()
        if sessions:
            print("Available sessions:")
            for session in sessions:
                print(f"ID: {session[0]}, Name: {session[1]}")
        else:
            print("No sessions available to join.")
```

exercise_manager.py
```python
'''
Manages practical exercises and feedback, allowing users to submit exercises and receive feedback.
'''
import tkinter as tk
import sqlite3
class ExerciseManager:
    def __init__(self, master):
        self.master = master
        self.frame = tk.Frame(self.master)
        self.frame.pack()
        self.db_connection = sqlite3.connect('exercises.db')
        self.create_table()
        self.exercise_name_entry = tk.Entry(self.frame)
    def create_table(self):
        # Create table for exercises if it doesn't exist
        with self.db_connection:
            self.db_connection.execute('''
                CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS exercises (
                    id INTEGER PRIMARY KEY AUTOINCREMENT,
                    exercise_name TEXT NOT NULL,
                    feedback TEXT
                )
            ''')
    def setup_ui(self):
        tk.Label(self.frame, text="Exercises", font=("Arial", 16)).pack()
        self.exercise_name_entry.pack()
        tk.Button(self.frame, text="Submit Exercise", command=self.submit_exercise).pack()
        tk.Button(self.frame, text="Get Feedback", command=self.provide_feedback).pack()
    def submit_exercise(self):
        # Logic to submit an exercise
        exercise_name = self.exercise_name_entry.get()
        if exercise_name:
            with self.db_connection:
                self.db_connection.execute('INSERT INTO exercises (exercise_name) VALUES (?)', (exercise_name,))
            print("Exercise submitted:", exercise_name)
        else:
            print("Please enter an exercise name.")
    def provide_feedback(self):
        # Logic to provide feedback
        cursor = self.db_connection.cursor()
        cursor.execute('SELECT * FROM exercises')
        exercises = cursor.fetchall()
        if exercises:
            for exercise in exercises:
                feedback = "Good job!"
                with self.db_connection:
                    self.db_connection.execute('UPDATE exercises SET feedback = ? WHERE id = ?', (feedback, exercise[0]))
                print(f"Feedback for {exercise[1]}: {feedback}")
        else:
            print("No exercises available for feedback.")
```

support_manager.py
```python
'''
Manages support for follow-up questions, allowing users to ask questions and receive answers.
'''
import tkinter as tk
import sqlite3
class SupportManager:
    def __init__(self, master):
        self.master = master
        self.frame = tk.Frame(self.master)
        self.frame.pack()
        self.db_connection = sqlite3.connect('support.db')
        self.create_table()
        self.question_entry = tk.Entry(self.frame)
    def create_table(self):
        # Create table for support questions if it doesn't exist
        with self.db_connection:
            self.db_connection.execute('''
                CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS support (
                    id INTEGER PRIMARY KEY AUTOINCREMENT,
                    question TEXT NOT NULL,
                    answer TEXT
                )
            ''')
    def setup_ui(self):
        tk.Label(self.frame, text="Support", font=("Arial", 16)).pack()
        self.question_entry.pack()
        tk.Button(self.frame, text="Ask Question", command=self.ask_question).pack()
        tk.Button(self.frame, text="Get Answer", command=self.provide_answer).pack()
    def ask_question(self):
        # Logic to ask a question
        question = self.question_entry.get()
        if question:
            with self.db_connection:
                self.db_connection.execute('INSERT INTO support (question) VALUES (?)', (question,))
            print("Question asked:", question)
        else:
            print("Please enter a question.")
    def provide_answer(self):
        # Logic to provide an answer
        cursor = self.db_connection.cursor()
        cursor.execute('SELECT * FROM support')
        questions = cursor.fetchall()
        if questions:
            for question in questions:
                answer = "Python is a programming language."
                with self.db_connection:
                    self.db_connection.execute('UPDATE support SET answer = ? WHERE id = ?', (answer, question[0]))
                print(f"Answer for '{question[1]}': {answer}")
        else:
            print("No questions available for answers.")
```

lesson_roadmap.py
```python
'''
Manages the lesson roadmap content and displays it in the GUI.
'''
import tkinter as tk
class LessonRoadmap:
    def __init__(self, master):
        self.master = master
        self.frame = tk.Frame(self.master)
        self.frame.pack()
    def load_roadmap(self):
        # Load roadmap from a file or database
        self.roadmap = [
            "1. Advanced Data Structures",
            "2. Object-Oriented Programming",
            "3. Functional Programming",
            "4. Concurrency and Parallelism",
            "5. Advanced Libraries and Frameworks",
            "6. Testing and Debugging",
            "7. Performance Optimization"
        ]
    def display_roadmap(self):
        self.load_roadmap()
        tk.Label(self.frame, text="Lesson Roadmap", font=("Arial", 16)).pack()
        for lesson in self.roadmap:
            tk.Label(self.frame, text=lesson).pack()
```

interactive_session.py
```python
'''
Handles live interactive sessions, allowing users to schedule and join sessions.
'''
import tkinter as tk
import sqlite3
class InteractiveSession:
    def __init__(self, master):
        self.master = master
        self.frame = tk.Frame(self.master)
        self.frame.pack()
        self.db_connection = sqlite3.connect('sessions.db')
        self.create_table()
        self.session_name_entry = tk.Entry(self.frame)
    def create_table(self):
        # Create table for sessions if it doesn't exist
        with self.db_connection:
            self.db_connection.execute('''
                CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS sessions (
                    id INTEGER PRIMARY KEY AUTOINCREMENT,
                    session_name TEXT NOT NULL
                )
            ''')
    def setup_ui(self):
        tk.Label(self.frame, text="Interactive Sessions", font=("Arial", 16)).pack()
        self.session_name_entry.pack()
        tk.Button(self.frame, text="Schedule Session", command=self.schedule_session).pack()
        tk.Button(self.frame, text="Join Session", command=self.join_session).pack()
    def schedule_session(self):
        # Logic to schedule a session
        session_name = self.session_name_entry.get()
        if session_name:
            with self.db_connection:
                self.db_connection.execute('INSERT INTO sessions (session_name) VALUES (?)', (session_name,))
            print("Session scheduled:", session_name)
        else:
            print("Please enter a session name.")
    def join_session(self):
        # Logic to join a session
        cursor = self.db_connection.cursor()
        cursor.execute('SELECT * FROM sessions')
        sessions = cursor.fetchall()
        if sessions:
            print("Available sessions:")
            for session in sessions:
                print(f"ID: {session[0]}, Name: {session[1]}")
        else:
            print("No sessions available to join.")
```

exercise_manager.py
```python
'''
Manages practical exercises and feedback, allowing users to submit exercises and receive feedback.
'''
import tkinter as tk
import sqlite3
class ExerciseManager:
    def __init__(self, master):
        self.master = master
        self.frame = tk.Frame(self.master)
        self.frame.pack()
        self.db_connection = sqlite3.connect('exercises.db')
        self.create_table()
        self.exercise_name_entry = tk.Entry(self.frame)
    def create_table(self):
        # Create table for exercises if it doesn't exist
        with self.db_connection:
            self.db_connection.execute('''
                CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS exercises (
                    id INTEGER PRIMARY KEY AUTOINCREMENT,
                    exercise_name TEXT NOT NULL,
                    feedback TEXT
                )
            ''')
    def setup_ui(self):
        tk.Label(self.frame, text="Exercises", font=("Arial", 16)).pack()
        self.exercise_name_entry.pack()
        tk.Button(self.frame, text="Submit Exercise", command=self.submit_exercise).pack()
        tk.Button(self.frame, text="Get Feedback", command=self.provide_feedback).pack()
    def submit_exercise(self):
        # Logic to submit an exercise
        exercise_name = self.exercise_name_entry.get()
        if exercise_name:
            with self.db_connection:
                self.db_connection.execute('INSERT INTO exercises (exercise_name) VALUES (?)', (exercise_name,))
            print("Exercise submitted:", exercise_name)
        else:
            print("Please enter an exercise name.")
    def provide_feedback(self):
        # Logic to provide feedback
        cursor = self.db_connection.cursor()
        cursor.execute('SELECT * FROM exercises')
        exercises = cursor.fetchall()
        if exercises:
            for exercise in exercises:
                feedback = "Good job!"
                with self.db_connection:
                    self.db_connection.execute('UPDATE exercises SET feedback = ? WHERE id = ?', (feedback, exercise[0]))
                print(f"Feedback for {exercise[1]}: {feedback}")
        else:
            print("No exercises available for feedback.")
```

support_manager.py
```python
'''
Manages support for follow-up questions, allowing users to ask questions and receive answers.
'''
import tkinter as tk
import sqlite3
class SupportManager:
    def __init__(self, master):
        self.master = master
        self.frame = tk.Frame(self.master)
        self.frame.pack()
        self.db_connection = sqlite3.connect('support.db')
        self.create_table()
        self.question_entry = tk.Entry(self.frame)
    def create_table(self):
        # Create table for support questions if it doesn't exist
        with self.db_connection:
            self.db_connection.execute('''
                CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS support (
                    id INTEGER PRIMARY KEY AUTOINCREMENT,
                    question TEXT NOT NULL,
                    answer TEXT
                )
            ''')
    def setup_ui(self):
        tk.Label(self.frame, text="Support", font=("Arial", 16)).pack()
        self.question_entry.pack()
        tk.Button(self.frame, text="Ask Question", command=self.ask_question).pack()
        tk.Button(self.frame, text="Get Answer", command=self.provide_answer).pack()
    def ask_question(self):
        # Logic to ask a question
        question = self.question_entry.get()
        if question:
            with self.db_connection:
                self.db_connection.execute('INSERT INTO support (question) VALUES (?)', (question,))
            print("Question asked:", question)
        else:
            print("Please enter a question.")
    def provide_answer(self):
        # Logic to provide an answer
        cursor = self.db_connection.cursor()
        cursor.execute('SELECT * FROM support')
        questions = cursor.fetchall()
        if questions:
            for question in questions:
                answer = "Python is a programming language."
                with self.db_connection:
                    self.db_connection.execute('UPDATE support SET answer = ? WHERE id = ?', (answer, question[0]))
                print(f"Answer for '{question[1]}': {answer}")
        else:
            print("No questions available for answers.")
```

```python
'''
Main application file that initializes and runs the Python skill advancement application.

import tkinter as tk
from lesson_roadmap import LessonRoadmap
from interactive_session import InteractiveSession
from exercise_manager import ExerciseManager
from support_manager import SupportManager

class MainApp:
    def __init__(self):
        self.root = tk.Tk()
        self.root.title("Python Skill Advancement")
        # Initialize components
        self.lesson_roadmap = LessonRoadmap(self.root)
        self.interactive_session = InteractiveSession(self.root)
        self.exercise_manager = ExerciseManager(self.root)
        self.support_manager = SupportManager(self.root)
        # Layout setup
        self.setup_ui()

    def setup_ui(self):
        # Setup UI components
        self.lesson_roadmap.display_roadmap()
        self.interactive_session.setup_ui()
        self.exercise_manager.setup_ui()
        self.support_manager.setup_ui()

    def run(self):
        self.root.mainloop()

if __name__ == "__main__":
    app = MainApp()
    app.run()
```

```python
'''
Manages support for follow-up questions, allowing users to ask questions and receive answers.

import tkinter as tk
import sqlite3

class SupportManager:
    def __init__(self, master):
        self.master = master
        self.frame = tk.Frame(self.master)
        self.frame.pack()
        self.db_connection = sqlite3.connect('support.db')
        self.create_table()
        self.question_entry = tk.Entry(self.frame)

    def create_table(self):
        # Create table for support questions if it doesn't exist
        with self.db_connection:
            self.db_connection.execute('''
                CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS support (
                    id INTEGER PRIMARY KEY AUTOINCREMENT,
                    question TEXT NOT NULL,
                    answer TEXT
                )
            ''')

    def setup_ui(self):
        tk.Label(self.frame, text="Support", font=("Arial", 16)).pack()
        self.question_entry.pack()
        tk.Button(self.frame, text="Ask Question", command=self.ask_question).pack()
        tk.Button(self.frame, text="Get Answer", command=self.provide_answer).pack()

    def ask_question(self):
        # Logic to ask a question
        question = self.question_entry.get()
        if question:
            with self.db_connection:
                self.db_connection.execute('INSERT INTO support (question) VALUES (?)', (question,))
            print("Question asked:", question)
        else:
            print("Please enter a question.")

    def provide_answer(self):
        # Logic to provide an answer
        cursor = self.db_connection.cursor()
        cursor.execute('SELECT * FROM support')
        questions = cursor.fetchall()
        if questions:
            for question in questions:
                answer = self.generate_answer(question[1])
                with self.db_connection:
                    self.db_connection.execute('UPDATE support SET answer = ? WHERE id = ?', (answer, question[0]))
                print(f"Answer for '{question[1]}': {answer}")
        else:
            print("No questions available for answers.")

    def generate_answer(self, question):
        # Generate a personalized answer based on the question
        return f"Answer for '{question}': Python is a versatile language used for many applications."
```

```python
        self.root = tk.Tk()

        # Initialize components
        self.lesson_roadmap = LessonRoadmap(self.root)
        self.interactive_session = InteractiveSession(self.root)

        self.support_manager = SupportManager(self.root)

        self.interactive_session.setup_ui()
        self.exercise_manager.setup_ui()
        self.support_manager.setup_ui()

if __name__ == "__main__":
```

```python
        self.question_entry.pack()
        tk.Button(self.frame, text="Ask Question", command=self.ask_question).pack()
        tk.Button(self.frame, text="Get Answer", command=self.provide_answer).pack()

    def ask_question(self):
        # Logic to ask a question
        question = self.question_entry.get()
        if question:
            with self.db_connection:
                self.db_connection.execute('INSERT INTO support (question) VALUES (?)', (question,))
            print("Question asked:", question)
        else:
            print("Please enter a question.")

    def provide_answer(self):
        # Logic to provide an answer
        cursor = self.db_connection.cursor()
        cursor.execute('SELECT * FROM support')
        questions = cursor.fetchall()
        if questions:
            for question in questions:
                answer = self.generate_answer(question[1])
                with self.db_connection:
                    self.db_connection.execute('UPDATE support SET answer = ? WHERE id = ?', (answer, question[0]))
                print(f"Answer for '{question[1]}': {answer}")
        else:
            print("No questions available for answers.")

    def generate_answer(self, question):
        # Generate a personalized answer based on the question
        return f"Answer for '{question}': Python is a versatile language used for many applications."
```

```python
'''
Main application file that initializes and runs the Python skill advancement application.
'''
import tkinter as tk
from lesson_roadmap import LessonRoadmap
from interactive_session import InteractiveSession
from exercise_manager import ExerciseManager
from support_manager import SupportManager
class MainApp:
    def __init__(self):
        self.root = tk.Tk()
        self.root.title("Python Skill Advancement")
        # Initialize components
        self.lesson_roadmap = LessonRoadmap(self.root)
        self.interactive_session = InteractiveSession(self.root)
        self.exercise_manager = ExerciseManager(self.root)
        self.support_manager = SupportManager(self.root)
        # Layout setup
        self.setup_ui()
    def setup_ui(self):
        # Setup UI components
        self.lesson_roadmap.display_roadmap()
        self.interactive_session.setup_ui()
        self.exercise_manager.setup_ui()
        self.support_manager.setup_ui()
    def run(self):
        self.root.mainloop()
if __name__ == "__main__":
    app = MainApp()
    app.run()
```

```python
'''
Manages the lesson roadmap content and displays it in the GUI.
'''
import tkinter as tk
class LessonRoadmap:
    def __init__(self, master):
        self.master = master
        self.frame = tk.Frame(self.master)
        self.frame.pack()
    def load_roadmap(self):
        # Load roadmap from a file or database
        self.roadmap = [
            "1. Advanced Data Structures",
            "2. Object-Oriented Programming",
            "3. Functional Programming",
            "4. Concurrency and Parallelism",
            "5. Advanced Libraries and Frameworks",
            "6. Testing and Debugging",
            "7. Performance Optimization"
        ]
    def display_roadmap(self):
        self.load_roadmap()
        tk.Label(self.frame, text="Lesson Roadmap", font=("Arial", 16)).pack()
        for lesson in self.roadmap:
            tk.Label(self.frame, text=lesson).pack()
```

interactive_session.py
```python
'''
Handles live interactive sessions, allowing users to schedule and join sessions.
'''
import tkinter as tk
import sqlite3
class InteractiveSession:
    def __init__(self, master):
        self.master = master
        self.frame = tk.Frame(self.master)
        self.frame.pack()
        self.db_connection = sqlite3.connect('sessions.db')
        self.create_table()
        self.session_name_entry = tk.Entry(self.frame)
    def create_table(self):
        # Create table for sessions if it doesn't exist
        with self.db_connection:
            self.db_connection.execute('''
                CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS sessions (
                    id INTEGER PRIMARY KEY AUTOINCREMENT,
                    session_name TEXT NOT NULL
                )
            ''')
    def setup_ui(self):
        tk.Label(self.frame, text="Interactive Sessions", font=("Arial", 16)).pack()
        self.session_name_entry.pack()
        tk.Button(self.frame, text="Schedule Session", command=self.schedule_session).pack()
        tk.Button(self.frame, text="Join Session", command=self.join_session).pack()
    def schedule_session(self):
        # Logic to schedule a session
        session_name = self.session_name_entry.get()
        if session_name:
            with self.db_connection:
                self.db_connection.execute('INSERT INTO sessions (session_name) VALUES (?)', (session_name,))
            print("Session scheduled:", session_name)
        else:
            print("Please enter a session name.")
    def join_session(self):
        # Logic to join a session
        cursor = self.db_connection.cursor()
        cursor.execute('SELECT * FROM sessions')
        sessions = cursor.fetchall()
        if sessions:
            print("Available sessions:")
            for session in sessions:
                print(f"ID: {session[0]}, Name: {session[1]}")
        else:
            print("No sessions available to join.")
```

exercise_manager.py
```python
'''
Manages practical exercises and feedback, allowing users to submit exercises and receive feedback.
'''
import tkinter as tk
import sqlite3
class ExerciseManager:
    def __init__(self, master):
        self.master = master
        self.frame = tk.Frame(self.master)
        self.frame.pack()
        self.db_connection = sqlite3.connect('exercises.db')
        self.create_table()
        self.exercise_name_entry = tk.Entry(self.frame)
    def create_table(self):
        # Create table for exercises if it doesn't exist
        with self.db_connection:
            self.db_connection.execute('''
                CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS exercises (
                    id INTEGER PRIMARY KEY AUTOINCREMENT,
                    exercise_name TEXT NOT NULL,
                    feedback TEXT
                )
            ''')
    def setup_ui(self):
        tk.Label(self.frame, text="Exercises", font=("Arial", 16)).pack()
        self.exercise_name_entry.pack()
        tk.Button(self.frame, text="Submit Exercise", command=self.submit_exercise).pack()
        tk.Button(self.frame, text="Get Feedback", command=self.provide_feedback).pack()
    def submit_exercise(self):
        # Logic to submit an exercise
        exercise_name = self.exercise_name_entry.get()
        if exercise_name:
            with self.db_connection:
                self.db_connection.execute('INSERT INTO exercises (exercise_name) VALUES (?)', (exercise_name,))
            print("Exercise submitted:", exercise_name)
        else:
            print("Please enter an exercise name.")
    def provide_feedback(self):
        # Logic to provide feedback
        cursor = self.db_connection.cursor()
        cursor.execute('SELECT * FROM exercises')
        exercises = cursor.fetchall()
        if exercises:
            for exercise in exercises:
                feedback = self.generate_feedback(exercise[1])
                with self.db_connection:
                    self.db_connection.execute('UPDATE exercises SET feedback = ? WHERE id = ?', (feedback, exercise[0]))
                print(f"Feedback for {exercise[1]}: {feedback}")
        else:
            print("No exercises available for feedback.")
    def generate_feedback(self, exercise_name):
        # Generate personalized feedback based on the exercise name
        return f"Feedback for {exercise_name}: Keep improving your skills!"
```

support_manager.py
```python
'''
Manages support for follow-up questions, allowing users to ask questions and receive answers.
'''
import tkinter as tk
import sqlite3
class SupportManager:
    def __init__(self, master):
        self.master = master
        self.frame = tk.Frame(self.master)
        self.frame.pack()
        self.db_connection = sqlite3.connect('support.db')
        self.create_table()
        self.question_entry = tk.Entry(self.frame)
    def create_table(self):
        # Create table for support questions if it doesn't exist
        with self.db_connection:
            self.db_connection.execute('''
                CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS support (
                    id INTEGER PRIMARY KEY AUTOINCREMENT,
                    question TEXT NOT NULL,
                    answer TEXT
                )
            ''')
    def setup_ui(self):
        tk.Label(self.frame, text="Support", font=("Arial", 16)).pack()
        self.question_entry.pack()
        tk.Button(self.frame, text="Ask Question", command=self.ask_question).pack()
        tk.Button(self.frame, text="Get Answer", command=self.provide_answer).pack()
    def ask_question(self):
        # Logic to ask a question
        question = self.question_entry.get()
        if question:
            with self.db_connection:
                self.db_connection.execute('INSERT INTO support (question) VALUES (?)', (question,))
            print("Question asked:", question)
        else:
            print("Please enter a question.")
    def provide_answer(self):
        # Logic to provide an answer
        cursor = self.db_connection.cursor()
        cursor.execute('SELECT * FROM support')
        questions = cursor.fetchall()
        if questions:
            for question in questions:
                answer = self.generate_answer(question[1])
                with self.db_connection:
                    self.db_connection.execute('UPDATE support SET answer = ? WHERE id = ?', (answer, question[0]))
                print(f"Answer for '{question[1]}': {answer}")
        else:
            print("No questions available for answers.")
    def generate_answer(self, question):
        # Generate a personalized answer based on the question
        return f"Answer for '{question}': Python is a versatile language used for many applications."
```

Based on the provided code, the project primarily uses the `tkinter` library for the GUI and `sqlite3` for database management. However, both `tkinter` and `sqlite3` are part of the Python Standard Library, so they do not need to be listed in the `requirements.txt` file.
```python
'''
Main application file that initializes and runs the Python skill advancement application.
'''
import tkinter as tk
from lesson_roadmap import LessonRoadmap
from interactive_session import InteractiveSession
from exercise_manager import ExerciseManager
from support_manager import SupportManager
class MainApp:
    def __init__(self):
        self.root = tk.Tk()
        self.root.title("Python Skill Advancement")
        # Initialize components
        self.lesson_roadmap = LessonRoadmap(self.root)
        self.interactive_session = InteractiveSession(self.root)
        self.exercise_manager = ExerciseManager(self.root)
        self.support_manager = SupportManager(self.root)
        # Layout setup
        self.setup_ui()
    def setup_ui(self):
        # Setup UI components
        self.lesson_roadmap.display_roadmap()
        self.interactive_session.setup_ui()
        self.exercise_manager.setup_ui()
        self.support_manager.setup_ui()
    def run(self):
        self.root.mainloop()
if __name__ == "__main__":
    app = MainApp()
    app.run()
```

lesson_roadmap.py
```python
'''
Manages the lesson roadmap content and displays it in the GUI.
'''
import tkinter as tk
class LessonRoadmap:
    def __init__(self, master):
        self.master = master
        self.frame = tk.Frame(self.master)
        self.frame.pack()
    def load_roadmap(self):
        # Load roadmap from a file or database
        self.roadmap = [
            "1. Advanced Data Structures",
            "2. Object-Oriented Programming",
            "3. Functional Programming",
            "4. Concurrency and Parallelism",
            "5. Advanced Libraries and Frameworks",
            "6. Testing and Debugging",
            "7. Performance Optimization"
        ]
    def display_roadmap(self):
        self.load_roadmap()
        tk.Label(self.frame, text="Lesson Roadmap", font=("Arial", 16)).pack()
        for lesson in self.roadmap:
            tk.Label(self.frame, text=lesson).pack()
```
