interactive_session.py
```python
'''
Handles live interactive sessions, allowing users to schedule and join sessions.
'''
import tkinter as tk
import sqlite3
class InteractiveSession:
    def __init__(self, master):
        self.master = master
        self.frame = tk.Frame(self.master)
        self.frame.pack()
        self.db_connection = sqlite3.connect('sessions.db')
        self.create_table()
        self.session_name_entry = tk.Entry(self.frame)
    def create_table(self):
        # Create table for sessions if it doesn't exist
        with self.db_connection:
            self.db_connection.execute('''
                CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS sessions (
                    id INTEGER PRIMARY KEY AUTOINCREMENT,
                    session_name TEXT NOT NULL
                )
            ''')
    def setup_ui(self):
        tk.Label(self.frame, text="Interactive Sessions", font=("Arial", 16)).pack()
        self.session_name_entry.pack()
        tk.Button(self.frame, text="Schedule Session", command=self.schedule_session).pack()
        tk.Button(self.frame, text="Join Session", command=self.join_session).pack()
    def schedule_session(self):
        # Logic to schedule a session
        session_name = self.session_name_entry.get()
        if session_name:
            with self.db_connection:
                self.db_connection.execute('INSERT INTO sessions (session_name) VALUES (?)', (session_name,))
            print("Session scheduled:", session_name)
        else:
            print("Please enter a session name.")
    def join_session(self):
        # Logic to join a session
        cursor = self.db_connection.cursor()
        cursor.execute('SELECT * FROM sessions')
        sessions = cursor.fetchall()
        if sessions:
            print("Available sessions:")
            for session in sessions:
                print(f"ID: {session[0]}, Name: {session[1]}")
        else:
            print("No sessions available to join.")
```
exercise_manager.py
```python
'''
Manages practical exercises and feedback, allowing users to submit exercises and receive feedback.
'''
import tkinter as tk
import sqlite3
class ExerciseManager:
    def __init__(self, master):
        self.master = master
        self.frame = tk.Frame(self.master)
        self.frame.pack()
        self.db_connection = sqlite3.connect('exercises.db')
        self.create_table()
        self.exercise_name_entry = tk.Entry(self.frame)
    def create_table(self):
        # Create table for exercises if it doesn't exist
        with self.db_connection:
            self.db_connection.execute('''
                CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS exercises (
                    id INTEGER PRIMARY KEY AUTOINCREMENT,
                    exercise_name TEXT NOT NULL,
                    feedback TEXT
                )
            ''')
    def setup_ui(self):
        tk.Label(self.frame, text="Exercises", font=("Arial", 16)).pack()
        self.exercise_name_entry.pack()
        tk.Button(self.frame, text="Submit Exercise", command=self.submit_exercise).pack()
        tk.Button(self.frame, text="Get Feedback", command=self.provide_feedback).pack()
    def submit_exercise(self):
        # Logic to submit an exercise
        exercise_name = self.exercise_name_entry.get()
        if exercise_name:
            with self.db_connection:
                self.db_connection.execute('INSERT INTO exercises (exercise_name) VALUES (?)', (exercise_name,))
            print("Exercise submitted:", exercise_name)
        else:
            print("Please enter an exercise name.")
    def provide_feedback(self):
        # Logic to provide feedback
        cursor = self.db_connection.cursor()
        cursor.execute('SELECT * FROM exercises')
        exercises = cursor.fetchall()
        if exercises:
            for exercise in exercises:
                feedback = self.generate_feedback(exercise[1])
                with self.db_connection:
                    self.db_connection.execute('UPDATE exercises SET feedback = ? WHERE id = ?', (feedback, exercise[0]))
                print(f"Feedback for {exercise[1]}: {feedback}")
        else:
            print("No exercises available for feedback.")
    def generate_feedback(self, exercise_name):
        # Generate personalized feedback based on the exercise name
        return f"Feedback for {exercise_name}: Keep improving your skills!"
```
support_manager.py
```python
'''
Manages support for follow-up questions, allowing users to ask questions and receive answers.
'''
import tkinter as tk
import sqlite3
class SupportManager:
    def __init__(self, master):
        self.master = master
        self.frame = tk.Frame(self.master)
        self.frame.pack()
        self.db_connection = sqlite3.connect('support.db')
        self.create_table()
        self.question_entry = tk.Entry(self.frame)
    def create_table(self):
        # Create table for support questions if it doesn't exist
        with self.db_connection:
            self.db_connection.execute('''
                CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS support (
                    id INTEGER PRIMARY KEY AUTOINCREMENT,
                    question TEXT NOT NULL,
                    answer TEXT
                )
            ''')
    def setup_ui(self):
        tk.Label(self.frame, text="Support", font=("Arial", 16)).pack()
        self.question_entry.pack()
        tk.Button(self.frame, text="Ask Question", command=self.ask_question).pack()
        tk.Button(self.frame, text="Get Answer", command=self.provide_answer).pack()
    def ask_question(self):
        # Logic to ask a question
        question = self.question_entry.get()
        if question:
            with self.db_connection:
                self.db_connection.execute('INSERT INTO support (question) VALUES (?)', (question,))
            print("Question asked:", question)
        else:
            print("Please enter a question.")
    def provide_answer(self):
        # Logic to provide an answer
        cursor = self.db_connection.cursor()
        cursor.execute('SELECT * FROM support')
        questions = cursor.fetchall()
        if questions:
            for question in questions:
                answer = self.generate_answer(question[1])
                with self.db_connection:
                    self.db_connection.execute('UPDATE support SET answer = ? WHERE id = ?', (answer, question[0]))
                print(f"Answer for '{question[1]}': {answer}")
        else:
            print("No questions available for answers.")
    def generate_answer(self, question):
        # Generate a personalized answer based on the question
        return f"Answer for '{question}': Python is a versatile language used for many applications."
```

```python
'''
Main application file that initializes and runs the Python skill advancement application.
'''
import tkinter as tk
from lesson_roadmap import LessonRoadmap
from interactive_session import InteractiveSession
from exercise_manager import ExerciseManager
from support_manager import SupportManager
class MainApp:
    def __init__(self):
        self.root = tk.Tk()
        self.root.title("Python Skill Advancement")
        # Initialize components
        self.lesson_roadmap = LessonRoadmap(self.root)
        self.interactive_session = InteractiveSession(self.root)
        self.exercise_manager = ExerciseManager(self.root)
        self.support_manager = SupportManager(self.root)
        # Layout setup
        self.setup_ui()
    def setup_ui(self):
        # Setup UI components
        self.lesson_roadmap.display_roadmap()
        self.interactive_session.setup_ui()
        self.exercise_manager.setup_ui()
        self.support_manager.setup_ui()
    def run(self):
        self.root.mainloop()
if __name__ == "__main__":
    app = MainApp()
    app.run()
```

lesson_roadmap.py
```python
'''
Manages the lesson roadmap content and displays it in the GUI.
'''
import tkinter as tk
class LessonRoadmap:
    def __init__(self, master):
        self.master = master
        self.frame = tk.Frame(self.master)
        self.frame.pack()
    def load_roadmap(self):
        # Load roadmap from a file or database
        self.roadmap = [
            "1. Advanced Data Structures",
            "2. Object-Oriented Programming",
            "3. Functional Programming",
            "4. Concurrency and Parallelism",
            "5. Advanced Libraries and Frameworks",
            "6. Testing and Debugging",
            "7. Performance Optimization"
        ]
    def display_roadmap(self):
        self.load_roadmap()
        tk.Label(self.frame, text="Lesson Roadmap", font=("Arial", 16)).pack()
        for lesson in self.roadmap:
            tk.Label(self.frame, text=lesson).pack()
```

interactive_session.py
```python
'''
Handles live interactive sessions, allowing users to schedule and join sessions.
'''
import tkinter as tk
import sqlite3
class InteractiveSession:
    def __init__(self, master):
        self.master = master
        self.frame = tk.Frame(self.master)
        self.frame.pack()
        self.db_connection = sqlite3.connect('sessions.db')
        self.create_table()
        self.session_name_entry = tk.Entry(self.frame)
    def create_table(self):
        # Create table for sessions if it doesn't exist
        with self.db_connection:
            self.db_connection.execute('''
                CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS sessions (
                    id INTEGER PRIMARY KEY AUTOINCREMENT,
                    session_name TEXT NOT NULL
                )
            ''')
    def setup_ui(self):
        tk.Label(self.frame, text="Interactive Sessions", font=("Arial", 16)).pack()
        self.session_name_entry.pack()
        tk.Button(self.frame, text="Schedule Session", command=self.schedule_session).pack()
        tk.Button(self.frame, text="Join Session", command=self.join_session).pack()
    def schedule_session(self):
        # Logic to schedule a session
        session_name = self.session_name_entry.get()
        if session_name:
            with self.db_connection:
                self.db_connection.execute('INSERT INTO sessions (session_name) VALUES (?)', (session_name,))
            print("Session scheduled:", session_name)
        else:
            print("Please enter a session name.")
    def join_session(self):
        # Logic to join a session
        cursor = self.db_connection.cursor()
        cursor.execute('SELECT * FROM sessions')
        sessions = cursor.fetchall()
        if sessions:
            print("Available sessions:")
            for session in sessions:
                print(f"ID: {session[0]}, Name: {session[1]}")
        else:
            print("No sessions available to join.")
```

exercise_manager.py
```python
'''
Manages practical exercises and feedback, allowing users to submit exercises and receive feedback.
'''
import tkinter as tk
import sqlite3
class ExerciseManager:
    def __init__(self, master):
        self.master = master
        self.frame = tk.Frame(self.master)
        self.frame.pack()
        self.db_connection = sqlite3.connect('exercises.db')
        self.create_table()
        self.exercise_name_entry = tk.Entry(self.frame)
    def create_table(self):
        # Create table for exercises if it doesn't exist
        with self.db_connection:
            self.db_connection.execute('''
                CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS exercises (
                    id INTEGER PRIMARY KEY AUTOINCREMENT,
                    exercise_name TEXT NOT NULL,
                    feedback TEXT
                )
            ''')
    def setup_ui(self):
        tk.Label(self.frame, text="Exercises", font=("Arial", 16)).pack()
        self.exercise_name_entry.pack()
        tk.Button(self.frame, text="Submit Exercise", command=self.submit_exercise).pack()
        tk.Button(self.frame, text="Get Feedback", command=self.provide_feedback).pack()
    def submit_exercise(self):
        # Logic to submit an exercise
        exercise_name = self.exercise_name_entry.get()
        if exercise_name:
            with self.db_connection:
                self.db_connection.execute('INSERT INTO exercises (exercise_name) VALUES (?)', (exercise_name,))
            print("Exercise submitted:", exercise_name)
        else:
            print("Please enter an exercise name.")
    def provide_feedback(self):
        # Logic to provide feedback
        cursor = self.db_connection.cursor()
        cursor.execute('SELECT * FROM exercises')
        exercises = cursor.fetchall()
        if exercises:
            for exercise in exercises:
                feedback = self.generate_feedback(exercise[1])
                with self.db_connection:
                    self.db_connection.execute('UPDATE exercises SET feedback = ? WHERE id = ?', (feedback, exercise[0]))
                print(f"Feedback for {exercise[1]}: {feedback}")
        else:
            print("No exercises available for feedback.")
    def generate_feedback(self, exercise_name):
        # Generate personalized feedback based on the exercise name
        return f"Feedback for {exercise_name}: Keep improving your skills!"
```

support_manager.py
```python
'''
Manages support for follow-up questions, allowing users to ask questions and receive answers.
'''
import tkinter as tk
import sqlite3
class SupportManager:
    def __init__(self, master):
        self.master = master
        self.frame = tk.Frame(self.master)
        self.frame.pack()
        self.db_connection = sqlite3.connect('support.db')
        self.create_table()
        self.question_entry = tk.Entry(self.frame)
    def create_table(self):
        # Create table for support questions if it doesn't exist
        with self.db_connection:
            self.db_connection.execute('''
                CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS support (
                    id INTEGER PRIMARY KEY AUTOINCREMENT,
                    question TEXT NOT NULL,
                    answer TEXT
                )
            ''')
    def setup_ui(self):
        tk.Label(self.frame, text="Support", font=("Arial", 16)).pack()
        self.question_entry.pack()
        tk.Button(self.frame, text="Ask Question", command=self.ask_question).pack()
        tk.Button(self.frame, text="Get Answer", command=self.provide_answer).pack()
    def ask_question(self):
        # Logic to ask a question
        question = self.question_entry.get()
        if question:
            with self.db_connection:
                self.db_connection.execute('INSERT INTO support (question) VALUES (?)', (question,))
            print("Question asked:", question)
        else:
            print("Please enter a question.")
    def provide_answer(self):
        # Logic to provide an answer
        cursor = self.db_connection.cursor()
        cursor.execute('SELECT * FROM support')
        questions = cursor.fetchall()
        if questions:
            for question in questions:
                answer = self.generate_answer(question[1])
                with self.db_connection:
                    self.db_connection.execute('UPDATE support SET answer = ? WHERE id = ?', (answer, question[0]))
                print(f"Answer for '{question[1]}': {answer}")
        else:
            print("No questions available for answers.")
    def generate_answer(self, question):
        # Generate a personalized answer based on the question
        return f"Answer for '{question}': Python is a versatile language used for many applications."
```
```

# LangChain

Building applications with LLMs through composability

Looking for the JS/TS version? Check out LangChain.js.

**Production Support:** As you move your LangChains into production, we'd love to offer more comprehensive support.

Please fill out this form and we'll set up a dedicated support Slack channel.

## Quick Install

`pip install langchain`

or

`conda install langchain -c conda-forge`

## 🤔 What is this?

Large language models (LLMs) are emerging as a transformative technology, enabling developers to build applications that they previously could not. However, using these LLMs in isolation is often insufficient for creating a truly powerful app - the real power comes when you can combine them with other sources of computation or knowledge.

This library aims to assist in the development of those types of applications. Common examples of these applications include:

**❓ Question Answering over specific documents**

- Documentation

- End-to-end Example: Question Answering over Notion Database

**🤖 Agents**

- Documentation

- End-to-end Example: GPT+WolframAlpha

## 📖 Documentation

Please see [here](https://python.langchain.com) for full documentation on:

- Getting started (installation, setting up the environment, simple examples)

- How-To examples (demos, integrations, helper functions)

- Reference (full API docs)

- Resources (high-level explanation of core concepts)
```

You are Chief Executive Officer. Now, we are both working at ChatDev and we share a common interest in collaborating to successfully complete a task assigned by a new customer.
Your main responsibilities include being an active decision-maker on users' demands and other key policy issues, leader, manager, and executor. Your decision-making role involves high-level decisions about policy and strategy; and your communicator role can involve speaking to the organization's management and employees.
Here is a new customer's task: Please help me create a personalized lesson roadmap for advancing Python skills from intermediate to advanced, incorporating live interactive sessions, practical exercises with feedback, and support for follow-up questions..
To complete the task, I will give you one or more instructions, and you must help me to write a specific solution that appropriately solves the requested instruction based on your expertise and my needs.]

# Python Skill Advancement Application

Welcome to the Python Skill Advancement Application, designed to help users advance their Python skills from intermediate to advanced levels. This application provides a comprehensive lesson roadmap, live interactive sessions, practical exercises with feedback, and support for follow-up questions.

## Main Features

1. **Lesson Roadmap**: A structured roadmap that guides users through advanced Python topics such as advanced data structures, object-oriented programming, functional programming, concurrency and parallelism, advanced libraries and frameworks, testing and debugging, and performance optimization.

2. **Interactive Sessions**: Users can schedule and join live interactive sessions to enhance their learning experience through real-time discussions and problem-solving.

3. **Exercise Manager**: Users can submit practical exercises and receive personalized feedback to improve their skills.

4. **Support Manager**: Users can ask follow-up questions and receive answers to clarify doubts and enhance their understanding.

## Quick Install

### Prerequisites

- Python 3.x
- Tkinter (usually included with Python)
- SQLite3 (usually included with Python)

### Installation

1. **Clone the Repository**: Clone the repository to your local machine using the following command:
   ```bash
   git clone <repository-url>
   ```

2. **Navigate to the Project Directory**: Change into the project directory:
   ```bash
   cd python-skill-advancement
   ```

3. **Install Dependencies**: There are no external dependencies required as of now. Ensure you have Python and Tkinter installed.

## How to Use

1. **Run the Application**: Start the application by running the `main.py` file:
   ```bash
   python main.py
   ```

2. **Explore the Lesson Roadmap**: The application will display a lesson roadmap. Navigate through the lessons to understand the topics covered.

3. **Schedule and Join Interactive Sessions**: Use the Interactive Sessions section to schedule new sessions or join existing ones. Enter a session name to schedule or view available sessions to join.

4. **Submit Exercises and Get Feedback**: In the Exercises section, submit exercises by entering an exercise name. Receive feedback to improve your skills.

5. **Ask Questions and Get Answers**: Use the Support section to ask questions and receive answers. Enter your question and view the answers provided.

## Additional Information

- **Database**: The application uses SQLite databases (`sessions.db`, `exercises.db`, `support.db`) to store session information, exercises, and support questions.

- **Feedback and Support**: For any issues or additional support, please contact our support team.

We hope this application helps you advance your Python skills effectively. Happy learning!
